tatarça</span></a></li><li class="interlanguage-link interwiki-shn mw-list-item"><a <ul style="line-height:100%; margin-left:1.35em;padding-left:0"><li>

For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">Help:IPA</a>.</td></tr></tbody></table>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><span><video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Mon_Thai_consonant.webm/220px--Mon_Thai_consonant.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="220" height="391" data-durationhint="34" data-mwtitle="Mon_Thai_consonant.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:Mon_Thai_consonant.webm"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/7/7d/Mon_Thai_consonant.webm/Mon_Thai_consonant.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; <p>The <b>Mon language</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <span class="ext-phonos"><span data-nosnippet="" id="ooui-php-1" class="ext-phonos-PhonosButton noexcerpt oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-buttonElement oo-ui-buttonElement-frameless oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-labelElement oo-ui-buttonWidget" data-ooui="{&quot;_&quot;:&quot;mw.Phonos.PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;href&quot;:&quot;\/\/upload.wikimedia.org\/wikipedia\/commons\/transcoded\/7\/77\/Mnw-%E1%80%98%E1%80%AC%E1%80%9E%E1%80%AC%E1%80%99%E1%80%94%E1%80%BA.oga\/Mnw-%E1%80%98%E1%80%AC%E1%80%9E%E1%80%AC%E1%80%99%E1%80%94%E1%80%BA.oga.mp3&quot;,&quot;rel&quot;:[&quot;nofollow&quot;],&quot;framed&quot;:false,&quot;icon&quot;:&quot;volumeUp&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:{&quot;html&quot;:&quot;listen&quot;},&quot;data&quot;:{&quot;ipa&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;lang&quot;:&quot;en&quot;,&quot;wikibase&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;file&quot;:&quot;Mnw-\u1018\u102c\u101e\u102c\u1019\u1014\u103a.oga&quot;},&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;noexcerpt&quot;]}"><a role="button" tabindex="0" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/7/77/Mnw-%E1%80%98%E1%80%AC%E1%80%9E%E1%80%AC%E1%80%99%E1%80%94%E1%80%BA.oga/Mnw-%E1%80%98%E1%80%AC%E1%80%9E%E1%80%AC%E1%80%99%E1%80%94%E1%80%BA.oga.mp3" rel="nofollow" aria-label="Play audio" title="Play audio" class="oo-ui-buttonElement-button"><span class="oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-volumeUp"></span><span class="oo-ui-labelElement-label">listen</span><span class="oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicatorElement-noIndicator"></span></a></span><sup class="ext-phonos-attribution noexcerpt navigation-not-searchable"><a href="/wiki/File:Mnw-%E1%80%98%E1%80%AC%E1%80%9E%E1%80%AC%E1%80%99%E1%80%94%E1%80%BA.oga" title="File:Mnw-ဘာသာမန်.oga">ⓘ</a></sup></span>; Mon: <span lang="mnw">ဘာသာမန်</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="mnw-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">&#91;pʰesa<span class="wrap"> </span>mɑn&#93;</a></span>; Mon-Thai <b>ဘာသာမည်</b> [<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">pʰiəsa<span class="wrap"> </span>moʊn</span>]; <a href="/wiki/Burmese_language" title="Burmese language">Burmese</a>: <span lang="my">မွန်ဘာသာ</span>; <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">ภาษามอญ</span>; formerly known as <b>Peguan</b> and <b>Talaing</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_languages" title="Austroasiatic languages">Austroasiatic language</a> spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Mon_people" title="Mon people">Mon people</a>. Mon, like the related <a href="/wiki/Khmer_language" title="Khmer language">Khmer language</a>, but unlike most languages in <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Southeast_Asia" title="Mainland Southeast Asia">mainland Southeast Asia</a>, is not tonal. The Mon language is a recognised indigenous language in Myanmar as well as a recognised indigenous <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Thailand" title="Languages of Thailand">language of Thailand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mon was classified as a "vulnerable" language in <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>'s 2010 <i><a href="/wiki/Red_Book_of_Endangered_Languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Book of Endangered Languages">Atlas of the World’s Languages in Danger</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The Mon language has faced assimilative pressures in both Myanmar and Thailand, where many individuals of Mon descent are now monolingual in Burmese or Thai respectively. In 2007, Mon speakers were estimated to number between 800,000 and 1 million.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In Myanmar, the majority of Mon speakers live in Southern Myanmar, especially <a href="/wiki/Mon_State" title="Mon State">Mon State</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Tanintharyi_Region" title="Tanintharyi Region">Tanintharyi Region</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kayin_State" title="Kayin State">Kayin State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<p>Mon is an important language in Burmese history. Until the 12th century, it was the <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Irrawaddy_River" title="Irrawaddy River">Irrawaddy valley</a>—not only in the Mon kingdoms of the lower Irrawaddy but also of the upriver <a href="/wiki/Pagan_Kingdom" title="Pagan Kingdom">Pagan Kingdom</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bamar_people" title="Bamar people">Bamar people</a>. Mon, especially written Mon, continued to be a <a href="/wiki/Prestige_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Prestige language">prestige language</a> even after the fall of the Mon <a href="/wiki/Thaton_Kingdom" title="Thaton Kingdom">kingdom of Thaton</a> to Pagan in 1057. King <a href="/wiki/Kyansittha" title="Kyansittha">Kyansittha</a> of Pagan (r. 1084–1113) admired Mon culture and the Mon language was patronized. 
</p>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Myazedi-Inscription-Mon.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Myazedi-Inscription-Mon.JPG/177px-Myazedi-Inscription-Mon.JPG" decoding="async" width="177" height="236" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Myazedi-Inscription-Mon.JPG/265px-Myazedi-Inscription-Mon.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Myazedi-Inscription-Mon.JPG/354px-Myazedi-Inscription-Mon.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>The Mon <a href="/wiki/Myazedi_Inscription" class="mw-redirect" title="Myazedi Inscription">Myazedi Inscription</a> (AD 1113) is Myanmar's oldest surviving stone inscription.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Kyansittha left many inscriptions in Mon. During this period, the <a href="/wiki/Myazedi_inscription" title="Myazedi inscription">Myazedi inscription</a>, which contains identical inscriptions of a story in <a href="/wiki/Pali" title="Pali">Pali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pyu_language_(Burma)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyu language (Burma)">Pyu</a>, Mon and Burmese on the four sides, was carved.<sup id="cite_ref-tarling_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tarling-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> However, after Kyansittha's death, usage of the Mon language declined among the Bamar and the <a href="/wiki/Burmese_language" title="Burmese language">Burmese language</a> began to replace Mon and Pyu as a <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tarling_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tarling-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mon inscriptions from <a href="/wiki/Dvaravati" title="Dvaravati">Dvaravati</a>'s ruins also litter <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>. However it is not clear if the inhabitants were Mon, a mix of Mon and Malay or Khmer. Later inscriptions and kingdoms like <a href="/wiki/Lavo_Kingdom" title="Lavo Kingdom">Lavo</a> were subservient to the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">Khmer Empire</a>.
</p><p>After the fall of Pagan, Mon again became the lingua franca of the <a href="/wiki/Hanthawaddy_Kingdom" title="Hanthawaddy Kingdom">Hanthawaddy Kingdom</a> (1287–1539) in present-day <a href="/wiki/Lower_Myanmar" title="Lower Myanmar">Lower Myanmar</a>, which remained a predominantly Mon-speaking region until the 1800s, by which point, the <a href="/wiki/Burmese_language" title="Burmese language">Burmese language</a> had expanded its reach from its traditional heartland in <a href="/wiki/Upper_Myanmar" title="Upper Myanmar">Upper Burma</a> into <a href="/wiki/Lower_Myanmar" title="Lower Myanmar">Lower Burma</a>.
</p><p>The region's language shift from Mon to Burmese has been ascribed to a combination of population displacement, intermarriage, and voluntary changes in self-identification among increasingly Mon–Burmese bilingual populations in throughout Lower Burma.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieberman2003202-206_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieberman2003202-206-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The shift was certainly accelerated by the fall of the Mon-speaking <a href="/wiki/Restored_Hanthawaddy_Kingdom" title="Restored Hanthawaddy Kingdom">Restored Hanthawaddy Kingdom</a> in 1757. Following the fall of Pegu (now Bago), many Mon-speaking refugees fled and resettled in what is now modern-day Thailand.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> By 1830, an estimated 90% of the population in the Lower Burma self-identified as Burmese-speaking Bamars; huge swaths of former Mon-speaking areas, from the <a href="/wiki/Irrawaddy_Delta" title="Irrawaddy Delta">Irrawaddy Delta</a> upriver, spanning Bassein (now Pathein) and Rangoon (now Yangon) to Tharrawaddy, Toungoo, Prome (now Pyay) and Henzada (now Hinthada), were now Burmese-speaking.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieberman2003202-206_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieberman2003202-206-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Great Britain's gradual annexation of Burma throughout the 19th century, in addition to concomitant economic and political instability in Upper Burma (e.g., increased tax burdens to the Burmese crown, British rice production incentives, etc.) also accelerated the migration of Burmese speakers from Upper Burma into Lower Burma.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Mon language has influenced subtle grammatical differences between the varieties of Burmese spoken in Lower and Upper Burma.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In Lower Burmese varieties, the verb ပေး ("to give") is colloquially used as a permissive causative marker, like in other Southeast Asian languages, but unlike in other Tibeto-Burman languages.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> This usage is hardly employed in Upper Burmese varieties, and is considered a sub-standard construct.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1972, the <a href="/wiki/New_Mon_State_Party" title="New Mon State Party">New Mon State Party</a> (NMSP) established a Mon national school system, which uses Mon as a <a href="/wiki/Medium_of_instruction" title="Medium of instruction">medium of instruction</a>, in rebel-controlled areas.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The system was expanded throughout Mon State following a ceasefire with the central government in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Mon State now operates a multi-track education system, with schools either using Mon as the primary medium of instruction (called Mon national schools) offering modules on the Mon language in addition to the government curriculum (called "mixed schools").<sup id="cite_ref-:0_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Mon language courses were launched state-wide at the elementary level.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> This system has been recognized as a model for <a href="/wiki/Mother-tongue" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother-tongue">mother-tongue</a> education in the Burmese national education system, because it enables children taught in the Mon language to integrate into the mainstream Burmese education system at higher education levels.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, it was announced that the <a href="/wiki/Mawlamyine" title="Mawlamyine">Mawlamyine</a>-based <i>Thanlwin Times</i> would begin to carry news in the Mon language, becoming Myanmar's first Mon language publication since 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution">Geographic distribution</span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mon_Thai_alphabet_in_Wat_Muang.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Mon_Thai_alphabet_in_Wat_Muang.jpg/220px-Mon_Thai_alphabet_in_Wat_Muang.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Mon_Thai_alphabet_in_Wat_Muang.jpg/330px-Mon_Thai_alphabet_in_Wat_Muang.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Mon_Thai_alphabet_in_Wat_Muang.jpg/440px-Mon_Thai_alphabet_in_Wat_Muang.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a><figcaption>Thai Mon and Thai scripts on a sign in Wat Muang, Thailand.</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mon_Thai_alphabet.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Mon_Thai_alphabet.jpg/220px-Mon_Thai_alphabet.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Mon_Thai_alphabet.jpg/330px-Mon_Thai_alphabet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Mon_Thai_alphabet.jpg/440px-Mon_Thai_alphabet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a><figcaption>Thai Mon and Thai scripts on a sign in Wat Muang, Thailand.</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mon_National_Day_in_Nakhon_Sawan.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Mon_National_Day_in_Nakhon_Sawan.jpg/220px-Mon_National_Day_in_Nakhon_Sawan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Mon_National_Day_in_Nakhon_Sawan.jpg/330px-Mon_National_Day_in_Nakhon_Sawan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Mon_National_Day_in_Nakhon_Sawan.jpg/440px-Mon_National_Day_in_Nakhon_Sawan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a><figcaption>Mon language in Thailand.</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><span><video id="mwe_player_2" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Wikipedia_20_marks_in_Mon.webm/220px--Wikipedia_20_marks_in_Mon.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="220" height="124" data-durationhint="121" data-mwtitle="Wikipedia_20_marks_in_Mon.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:Wikipedia_20_marks_in_Mon.webm"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/d/de/Wikipedia_20_marks_in_Mon.webm/Wikipedia_20_marks_in_Mon.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; <p>Southern Myanmar (comprising <a href="/wiki/Mon_State" title="Mon State">Mon State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kayin_State" title="Kayin State">Kayin State</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tanintharyi_Region" title="Tanintharyi Region">Tanintharyi Region</a>), from the <a href="/wiki/Sittaung_River" title="Sittaung River">Sittaung River</a> in the north to <a href="/wiki/Myeik,_Myanmar" title="Myeik, Myanmar">Myeik</a> (Mergui) and <a href="/wiki/Kawthaung" title="Kawthaung">Kawthaung</a> in the south, remains a traditional stronghold of the Mon language.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> However, in this region, Burmese is favored in urban areas, such as <a href="/wiki/Mawlamyine" title="Mawlamyine">Mawlamyine</a>, the capital of Mon State.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In recent years, usage of Mon has declined in Myanmar, especially among the younger generation.<sup id="cite_ref-ethno_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethno-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While Thailand is home to a sizable Mon population due to historical waves of migration, only a small proportion (estimated to range between 60,000 and 80,000) speak Mon, due to <a href="/wiki/Thaification" title="Thaification">Thaification</a> and the assimilation of Mons into mainstream Thai society.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Mon speakers in Thailand are largely concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Ko_Kret" title="Ko Kret">Ko Kret</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:3_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The remaining contingent of Thai Mon speakers are located in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Samut_Sakhon_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Samut Sakhon Province">Samut Sakhon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samut_Songkhram_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Samut Songkhram Province">Samut Songkhram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nakhon_Pathom_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Nakhon Pathom Province">Nakhon Pathom</a>, as well the western provinces bordering Myanmar (<a href="/wiki/Kanchanaburi" title="Kanchanaburi">Kanchanaburi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phetchaburi" title="Phetchaburi">Phetchaburi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prachuap_Khiri_Khan" title="Prachuap Khiri Khan">Prachuap Khiri Khan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ratchaburi" title="Ratchaburi">Ratchaburi</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-:3_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> A small ethnic group in Thailand speak a language closely related to Mon, called <a href="/wiki/Nyah_Kur_language" title="Nyah Kur language">Nyah Kur</a>. They are descendants of the Mon-speaking <a href="/wiki/Dvaravati" title="Dvaravati">Dvaravati</a> kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">Dialects</span></h2>
<p>Mon has three primary dialects in Burma, coming from the various regions the Mon inhabit. They are the Central (areas surrounding <a href="/wiki/Mottama" title="Mottama">Mottama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mawlamyine" title="Mawlamyine">Mawlamyine</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bago,_Myanmar" title="Bago, Myanmar">Bago</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ye,_Mon_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Ye, Mon State">Ye</a> dialects.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> All are mutually intelligible. <i>Ethnologue</i> lists Mon dialects as Martaban-Moulmein (Central Mon, Mon Te), Pegu (Mon Tang, Northern Mon), and Ye (Mon Nya, Southern Mon), with high mutual intelligibility among them.
</p><p>Thai Mon has some differences from the Burmese dialects of Mon, but they are mutually intelligible. The Thai varieties of Mon are considered "severely endangered."<sup id="cite_ref-:4_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocalic_register">Vocalic register</span></h3>
<p>Unlike the surrounding Burmese and <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a> languages, Mon is not a <a href="/wiki/Tone_(linguistics)" title="Tone (linguistics)">tonal language</a>. As in many Mon–Khmer languages, Mon uses a vowel-phonation or vowel-<a href="/wiki/Register_(phonology)" title="Register (phonology)">register</a> system in which the quality of voice in pronouncing the vowel is phonemic. There are two registers in Mon:
</p>
<ol><li>Clear (modal) voice, analyzed by various linguists as ranging from ordinary to <a href="/wiki/Creaky_voice" title="Creaky voice">creaky</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Breathy_voice" title="Breathy voice">Breathy voice</a>, vowels have a distinct breathy quality</li></ol>
<p>One study involving speakers of a Mon dialect in Thailand found that in some syllabic environments, words with a breathy voice vowel are significantly lower in pitch than similar words with a clear vowel counterpart.<sup id="cite_ref-thongkum_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thongkum-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> While difference in pitch in certain environments was found to be significant, there are no <a href="/wiki/Minimal_pair" title="Minimal pair">minimal pairs</a> that are distinguished solely by pitch. The contrastive mechanism is the vowel phonation.
</p><p>In the examples below, breathy voice is marked with under-diaeresis.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verbs_and_verb_phrases">Verbs and verb phrases</span></h3>
<p>Mon verbs do not inflect for person. Tense is shown through particles.
</p><p>Some verbs have a morphological causative, which is most frequently a /pə-/ prefix (Pan Hla 1989:29):
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th>Underived verb</th>
<th>Gloss</th>
<th>Causative verb</th>
<th>Gloss
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>c<sup>h</sup>ɒt</td>
<td>to die</td>
<td>kəcɒt</td>
<td>to kill
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>lɜm</td>
<td>to be ruined</td>
<td>pəlɒm</td>
<td>to destroy
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>k<sup>h</sup>aɨŋ</td>
<td>to be firm</td>
<td>pəkhaɨŋ</td>
<td>to make firm
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>tɛm</td>
<td>to know</td>
<td>pətɛm</td>
<td>to inform
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nouns_and_noun_phrases">Nouns and noun phrases</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Singular_and_plural">Singular and plural</span></h4>
<p>Mon nouns do not inflect for number. That is, they do not have separate forms for singular and plural:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sɔt pakaw</p><p style="margin: 0px;">apple</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mo̤a</p><p style="margin: 0px;">one</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">me̤a</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="classifier" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CL</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">{sɔt pakaw} mo̤a me̤a</p><p style="display: none;">apple one CL</p><p style="clear: left;">'one apple'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sɔt pakaw</p><p style="margin: 0px;">apple</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ba</p><p style="margin: 0px;">two</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">me̤a</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="classifier" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CL</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">{sɔt pakaw} ba me̤a</p><p style="display: none;">apple two CL</p><p style="clear: left;">'two apples'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjectives">Adjectives</span></h4>
<p>Adjectives follow the noun (Pan Hla p.&#160;24):
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">prɛ̤a</p><p style="margin: 0px;">woman</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ce</p><p style="margin: 0px;">beautiful</p></div><p style="display: none;">prɛ̤a ce</p><p style="display: none;">woman beautiful</p><p style="clear: left;">'beautiful woman'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Demonstratives">Demonstratives</span></h4>
<p>Demonstratives follow the noun:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ŋoa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">day</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nɔʔ</p><p style="margin: 0px;">this</p></div><p style="display: none;">ŋoa nɔʔ</p><p style="display: none;">day this</p><p style="clear: left;">this day</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Classifiers">Classifiers</span></h4>
<p>Like many other Southeast Asian languages, Mon has <a href="/wiki/Classifier_(linguistics)" title="Classifier (linguistics)">classifiers</a> which are used when a noun appears with a numeral. The choice of classifier depends on the semantics of the noun involved.
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kaneh</p><p style="margin: 0px;">pen</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mo̤a</p><p style="margin: 0px;">one</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tanəng</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="classifier" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CL</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">kaneh mo̤a tanəng</p><p style="display: none;">pen one CL</p><p style="clear: left;">'one pen'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">chup</p><p style="margin: 0px;">tree</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mo̤a</p><p style="margin: 0px;">one</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tanɒm</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="classifier" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CL</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">chup mo̤a tanɒm</p><p style="display: none;">tree one CL</p><p style="clear: left;">'one tree'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prepositions_and_prepositional_phrases">Prepositions and prepositional phrases</span></h3>
<p>Mon is a prepositional language.
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">doa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">in</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">əma</p><p style="margin: 0px;">lake</p></div><p style="display: none;">doa əma</p><p style="display: none;">in lake</p><p style="clear: left;">'in the lake'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sentences">Sentences</span></h3>
<p>The ordinary word order for sentences in Mon is subject–verb–object, as in the following examples
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;"><span style="font-family: Pyidaungsu, TharLon, &#39;Noto Sans Myanmar&#39;, &#39;Myanmar Text&#39;;">အဲ</span></p><p lang="mnw-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ʔoa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">I</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;"><span style="font-family: Pyidaungsu, TharLon, &#39;Noto Sans Myanmar&#39;, &#39;Myanmar Text&#39;;">ရာန်</span></p><p lang="mnw-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ran</p><p style="margin: 0px;">buy</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;"><span style="font-family: Pyidaungsu, TharLon, &#39;Noto Sans Myanmar&#39;, &#39;Myanmar Text&#39;;">သ္ၚု</span></p><p lang="mnw-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">hau</p><p style="margin: 0px;">rice</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;"><span style="font-family: Pyidaungsu, TharLon, &#39;Noto Sans Myanmar&#39;, &#39;Myanmar Text&#39;;">တုဲ</span></p><p lang="mnw-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">toa</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="completive aspect" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">COMPL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;"><span style="font-family: Pyidaungsu, TharLon, &#39;Noto Sans Myanmar&#39;, &#39;Myanmar Text&#39;;">ယျ</span></p><p lang="mnw-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ya.</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="affirmative" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Questions">Questions</span></h3>
<p>Yes–no questions are shown with a final particle <i>ha</i>
</p>

margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;"><span style="font-family: Pyidaungsu, TharLon, &#39;Noto Sans Myanmar&#39;, &#39;Myanmar Text&#39;;">စ</span></p><p lang="mnw-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">shea</p><p style="margin: 0px;">eat</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;"><span style="font-family: Pyidaungsu, TharLon, &#39;Noto Sans Myanmar&#39;, &#39;Myanmar Text&#39;;">ပုင်</span></p><p lang="mnw-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">pəng</p><p <p>Wh-questions show a different final particle, <i>rau</i>. The interrogative word does not undergo <a href="/wiki/Wh-movement" title="Wh-movement">wh-movement</a>. That is, it does not necessarily move to the front of the sentence:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;"><span style="font-family: Pyidaungsu, TharLon, &#39;Noto Sans Myanmar&#39;, &#39;Myanmar Text&#39;;">တၠ နာဲ</span></p><p lang="mnw-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Tala oa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">You</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;"><span style="font-family: Pyidaungsu, TharLon, &#39;Noto Sans Myanmar&#39;, &#39;Myanmar Text&#39;;">ကြာတ်ကြဴ</span>မံင်</p><p lang="mnw-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kratkraw</p><p style="margin: 0px;">wash</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;"><span style="font-family: Pyidaungsu, TharLon, &#39;Noto Sans Myanmar&#39;, &#39;Myanmar Text&#39;;">မူ</span></p><p lang="mnw-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mu</p><p style="margin: 0px;">what</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mnw" style="margin: 0px;"><span style="font-family: Pyidaungsu, TharLon, &#39;Noto Sans Myanmar&#39;, &#39;Myanmar Text&#39;;">ရော</span></p><p lang="mnw-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">raw?</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="wh-question" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">WH</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="question word" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">Q</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p
